  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5042688914701027829">Terry Pratchett's profoundly irreverent novels are consistent number one bestsellers in England, where they have garnered him a revered position in the halls of parody next to Mark Twain, Kurt Vonnegut, Douglas Adams, and Carl Hiaasen.<br /><br />The Color of Magic is Terry Pratchett's maiden voyage through the now-legendary land of Discworld. QUOTE page 63 "This is the author saying this, folks.<a href="#" class="jsShow showAction">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I am currently reading "A Slip of the Keyboard" A collection of non-fiction by Terry Pratchett. QUOTE page 63 "This is the author saying this, folks. Do not start at the beginning with Discworld" although he does not say which one to start with. Ive read a few but did not start at the beginning n reading Terry Pratchett saying don't start at the beginning I'm glad I never. <a href="#" class="jsHide hideAction">(less)</a></span></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_214129132">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/214129132" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence" class="left imgcol" title="Mark Lawrence"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442536170p2/4508542.jpg" alt="Mark Lawrence" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/214129132?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 09, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence" class="user" title="Mark Lawrence">Mark Lawrence</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/601238.The_Colour_of_Magic" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780552124751" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer214129132">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14235855654428638969">I haven't reviewed this because I read it so long ago that all I can remember is I loved it.<br /><br />I'll take our very old and battered copy (bought in 1987) to the hospice this weekend when I go with Celyn and see if I can't refresh my memory.<br /><br />RIP, Sir Terry.<br /><br />'DON'T THINK OF IT AS DYING,' said Death, 'JUST THINK OF IT AS LEAVING EARLY TO AVOID THE RUSH.'<br /><br /><br />So - to the review!<br /><br />I've just read this in slightly over 24 hours ... which is extraordinary for me. I normally take a month to read a book. <br /><br />It is, to be</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14235855654428638969">I haven't reviewed this because I read it so long ago that all I can remember is I loved it.<br /><br />I'll take our very old and battered copy (bought in 1987) to the hospice this weekend when I go with Celyn and see if I can't refresh my memory.<br /><br />RIP, Sir Terry.<br /><br />'DON'T THINK OF IT AS DYING,' said Death, 'JUST THINK OF IT AS LEAVING EARLY TO AVOID THE RUSH.'<br /><br /><br />So - to the review!<br /><br />I've just read this in slightly over 24 hours ... which is extraordinary for me. I normally take a month to read a book. <br /><br />It is, to be fair, both a very readable and a very short book (65,000 words - a short fantasy these days is ~100,000 words).<br /><br />I was surprised to find how much of this I remembered, especially as I last read it 28 years ago!<br /><br />It's a very funny book with some GREAT one-liners. I particularly liked one that said about men falling foul of the thieves' guild (I paraphrase) '... men who wouldn't be going home again ... unless they happened to live near the river and their corpses floated by on the way to the sea."<br /><br />And this from the character Twoflower was poignant:<br /><br />"When I think that I might die without seeing a hundredth of all there is to see it makes me feel," he paused, then added, "well, humble, I suppose. And very angry, of course." <br /><br /><br />Anyway - incompetent and cowardly failed wizard Rincewind falls in with Twoflower, the naive tourist with an impossibly optimistic attitude, oodles of gold, and an indestructible, vicious and implacable treasure chest on legs to defend him.<br /><br />Hilarity ensues as Twoflower tries to see everything, Rincewind tries not to die, and the gods play games with them. We get a great tour of the Discworld, its geography, magics, and inhabitants, all of which are so fantastically imaginative and amusing that even geography becomes a joy.<br /><br />This isn't Terry Pratchett's best book but it's full of all the great stuff that gathers together into its peak a few books into the series. It's certainly an excellent book though. Pratchett has an incredibly rare talent for compressing humour into one-liners that are witty, incisive, and yet never feel mean - it's not jokes that you feel are directed _at_ anyone, just mined from the stuff of life.<br /><br />I had a great time revisiting this book and if you've not tried it - now's the time!<br /><br /><br />.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14235855654428638969">...more</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10923016-david-proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party" class="user" title="David &quot;proud Gleeman in Branwen's adventuring party&quot;">David "proud Gleeman in Branwen's adventuring party"</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic" title="Hardcover 9780060855925" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/10923016-david-proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10923016-david-proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=make-me-laugh" class="actionLinkLite">make-me-laugh</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10923016-david-proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=2013-reads" class="actionLinkLite">2013-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer438656859">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8430559344407353871"><em>Reading </em><strong>The Color of Magic</strong><em> is akin to eating an entire bowl of ice cream just a little too fast...sure, it may cause your head to hurt at times, but the sweet rewards make it all worth it!</em><br /><br />Filled with ambitious wizards and ruthless assassins, the city of Ankh-Morpork has survived many dangers in the past, but now it faces an even more destructive force...<em>TOURISM</em>!!! When a rich but bored outsider named Twoflower decides to explore the city in search for adventure, it soon becomes an adventure for</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8430559344407353871"><em>Reading </em><strong>The Color of Magic</strong><em> is akin to eating an entire bowl of ice cream just a little too fast...sure, it may cause your head to hurt at times, but the sweet rewards make it all worth it!</em><br /><br />Filled with ambitious wizards and ruthless assassins, the city of Ankh-Morpork has survived many dangers in the past, but now it faces an even more destructive force...<em>TOURISM</em>!!! When a rich but bored outsider named Twoflower decides to explore the city in search for adventure, it soon becomes an adventure for everyone around him, too! Twoflower's well-meaning but careless ways earn him the attention of pirates, dragonriders, and various supernatural entities, all looking to rid Twoflower of his treasure...not to mention his life! Soon failed wizard Rincewind reluctantly becomes Twoflower's guide, and as Twoflower explores more and more of Discworld looking for the adventure of a lifetime, Rincewind tries desperately to make sure his lifetime lasts for more than five minutes!<br /><br />This was me for about 80% of this book...<br /><img width="300" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="homerlaugh" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395015i/760698.jpg" /><br /><br /><em>Annnnnd</em> here I am for the other 20%....<br /><img width="300" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="homerconfused" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395015i/760699.png" /><br /><br />What I loved most about this book was definitely the humor. Some authors can only come up with a great laugh-out-loud moment once or twice in a book, but Pratchett is able to pull one off in just about every page! There are oodles of witty dialogue all throughout the novel, as well as some great slapstick moments. In addition, Pratchett gives us some excellent satire, too. I got a big kick out of how familiar some of Twoflower's ideas were, like when he convinces a bar owner to "place a bet" on whether or not the bar will be damaged...Twoflower calls this process <em>"inn-sewer-ants"</em>! By having the other characters mock the "outrageous" concepts Twoflower introduces them to, it did a magnificent job painting an amusing picture of some of the absurdities of everyday life. "The Color of Magic" isn't just a humorous book, it actually manages to pull off several different kinds of humor!<br /><br />Also, I was amazed with the extent of Pratchett's imagination! While some elements of this book are your standard fantasy archetypes, Pratchett really ups the ante by giving us some brilliantly creative concepts as well. With translucent dragons, trolls made out of water, a sentient piece of luggage that manages to display so much personality without ever saying a word, and an upside-down swordfight that has to be <s>seen</s>, errr, <strong>read</strong> to be believed, Pratchett never runs out of new ideas to entertain his audience with.<br /><br />Alas, while I enjoyed this book very much, I did have a couple of issues with it. For one thing, I felt like Pratchett tried to cram way too much into a book that's barely over 200 pages. So many characters and creatures come and go, it quickly becomes difficult to keep track of what's going on! I have some friends who didn't enjoy the "Game of Thrones" book as they found it confusing, but at least George R.R. Martin takes a good amount of time to establish all the characters, whereas this book can sometimes feel like trying to watch a NASCAR race where all the cars are speeding in a different direction! Also, some of Pratchett's ideas were a little too <em>"out-there"</em> for me...I knew this was going to be a problem right away, when Pratchett begins the book by revealing that Discworld is a planet that is carried on the backs of four elephants who are all standing on the shell of a giant turtle that is floating through space...<br /><img width="350" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="discworld" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395015i/760700._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><em>"This is an awful lot to throw at me on page one, Mr. Pratchett!"</em><br /><br />Also, while "The Color of Magic" works beautifully as a comedy, I'm afraid the actual story doesn't quite hit the mark. The book is divided into four parts, and each part feels like a separate book. Almost anyone introduced in one section is absent in the other three, so we're left wondering what happened to many different characters. While the events of Rincewind's and Twoflower's journey are fun to watch, there's very little true progression or closure. This storytelling technique was especially baffling in the fourth segment, where Pratchett keeps referring to an adventure that we never got to see, as it occurred inbetween the third and fourth sections. This disjointed method of storytelling prevented the book from becoming anything more than just a comedy of errors, as amusing as those errors may have been.<br /><br />So, while I felt this book would have been better if it were a bit longer and some of the concepts had been more fleshed out, I still had a lot of fun reading this hysterically funny adventure. I've been told that the first couple of books in the Discworld series pale in comparison to the later ones. Considering how entertaining "The Color of Magic" was, if this truly is one of the weaker entries, I can't wait to read more of the Discworld series! <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8430559344407353871">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5358354640192304599">While I love Discworld series, I've got to say that 'The Color of Magic' suffers from what I call 'First Book Syndrom' - the author has to establish t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5358354640192304599">While I love Discworld series, I've got to say that 'The Color of Magic' suffers from what I call 'First Book Syndrom' - the author has to establish the world and the characters, and as a result the book becomes too crammed in some aspects (all the bizzare fantasy things) and not fleshed out in others (the actual plot). However, the next books fill in the gap nicely; in fact, the next book 'The Light Fantastic' acts as a direct sequel, continuing from the very point 'The Color of Magic' ends. In a way, it's like a one long book, and it's plot is much stronger than just hopping from adventure to adventure that we have there. So I hope you will enjoy next books even more - I know that I did! ;)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5358354640192304599">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_62840867">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62840867" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1022982-brad" class="left imgcol" title="Brad"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" alt="Brad" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/62840867?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 29, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1022982-brad" class="user" title="Brad">Brad</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/601238.The_Colour_of_Magic" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780552124751" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=speculative" class="actionLinkLite">speculative</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=sci-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">sci-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=political" class="actionLinkLite">political</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=doing-the-dishes" class="actionLinkLite">doing-the-dishes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer62840867">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5748537769150180059">Before picking it up, I'd heard that <a title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1_">The Colour of Magic</a> was funny. Now that can mean just about anything because, let's face it, comedy is the most subjective of arts. <br /><br />Funny is a deeply personal thing. The "funny peculiar" and the "funny ha-ha" might not be the same from person to person or even to the same person depending on their mood or their place in life. So knowing something is funny ahead of reading it really doesn't tell me much. <br /><br />I'd read <a title="Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">Terry Pratchett</a>'s &amp; <a title="Neil Gaiman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1221698.Neil_Gaiman">Neil Gaiman</a>'s <a title="Good Omens The Nice and Accurate Prophecies of Agnes Nutter, Witch by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12067.Good_Omens_The_Nice_and_Accurate_Prophecies_of_Agnes_Nutter__Witch">Good Omen</a></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5748537769150180059">Before picking it up, I'd heard that <a title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1_">The Colour of Magic</a> was funny. Now that can mean just about anything because, let's face it, comedy is the most subjective of arts. <br /><br />Funny is a deeply personal thing. The "funny peculiar" and the "funny ha-ha" might not be the same from person to person or even to the same person depending on their mood or their place in life. So knowing something is funny ahead of reading it really doesn't tell me much. <br /><br />I'd read <a title="Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">Terry Pratchett</a>'s &amp; <a title="Neil Gaiman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1221698.Neil_Gaiman">Neil Gaiman</a>'s <a title="Good Omens The Nice and Accurate Prophecies of Agnes Nutter, Witch by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12067.Good_Omens_The_Nice_and_Accurate_Prophecies_of_Agnes_Nutter__Witch">Good Omens</a> quite a while ago, so I expected at least a hint of satire and politically conscious wit, but I had no idea which of the authors to blame for the smart laughs in <a title="Good Omens The Nice and Accurate Prophecies of Agnes Nutter, Witch by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12067.Good_Omens_The_Nice_and_Accurate_Prophecies_of_Agnes_Nutter__Witch">Good Omens</a>, and my recollections really shed no illumination on what was to come. So I read <a title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1_">The Colour of Magic</a> with as open a mind as I could and hoped for some laughs. <br /><br />I didn't laugh much and that surprised me. I smiled an awful lot, though. But I didn't laugh. No out loud snickers; no full-out belly laughs; no snorts; no giggles. <br /><br />But I did smile. <br /><br />Pratchett's kooky tale (really four tales to make one) of Rincewind, the one-great-spell, wizarding failure, Twoflower, the in-sewer-ants adjuster/tourist, and his Luggage was smart more often than it was stupid, consciously political, satirically silly, more than willing to take the piss out of Fantasy as a genre, but mostly it was exceedingly absurd. And all of this was what made <a title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1_">The Colour of Magic</a> good to very good. <br /><br />Even so, its audience is necessarily limited. I know why I liked <a title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1_">The Colour of Magic</a>, and while I imagine there are other reasons to like the story, I think it is probably a fairly inaccessible tale unless you are a reader who falls into a niche of accessibility. This is not a book that can be widely read or widely liked. <br /><br />So why did I like it? I liked it because I fall into a niche wherein I was able to access memories of drunken, drug-addled, teenage D&amp;D marathons (which were extremely rare since we preferred our gaming sober), where we gave up being serious and descended into near madness. <br /><br />Those nights are reflected in everything that happens in <a title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1_">The Colour of Magic</a>. Obligatory bar fights of fantastic impossibility, Monty Hall swords and treasures, idiotic last second rescues, gods dicing, heroes thinking with the dirk in their pants, dimensional slips and deus ex machinas at every turn make <a title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1_">The Colour of Magic</a> a collage of gaming stupidity, and it was nice to take a nostalgic trip back to my adolescence. In fact, Pratchett captures exactly the sort of gaming experience that led our halfling priest of Xyice, God of Mischief, to wish for a foot long penis then fall unconscious from blood loss when he achieved his first erection. So I liked this book...a lot, actually.<br /><br />But it wasn't the best story I've ever read, and I can't imagine I could sit down and read the entire Discworld cycle without a break. It's fun. It's light. Pratchett writes better than I expected, but I bet there are many folks out there who hate this book. You have my sympathy. <br /><br />So yes...I was disappointed that I didn't laugh more; I was disappointed that the story wasn't more subtle; I hated the turtle carrying the disc; I wanted <a title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1_">The Colour of Magic</a> to be more biting than silly, more critical than absurd, more intelligent than clever. But it was a fun ride that entertained me while I did the dishes, and I couldn't help liking Rincewind, so I will probably go on, and I will likely become a fan of Pratchett's Discworld books...in spite of themselves. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5748537769150180059">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_28987780">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/28987780" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1385106-jamie" class="left imgcol" title="Jamie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1217535570p2/1385106.jpg" alt="Jamie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/28987780?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 01, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1385106-jamie" class="user" title="Jamie">Jamie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic" title="Hardcover 9780060855925" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer28987780">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2932020423926860904">I'm pretty sure people have told me about Pratchett and his Diskworld series before, usually working in the phrase "He's the Douglas Adams of fantasy" into the description. But the problem was that I always felt that I had had enough of Adams after the third Hithiker's Guide to the Galaxy book, and whenever I scanned Pratchett's section in the bookstore I was immediately put off by not knowing where to start reading among the approximately five hundred thousand Diskworld books. I'm glad I finall</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2932020423926860904">I'm pretty sure people have told me about Pratchett and his Diskworld series before, usually working in the phrase "He's the Douglas Adams of fantasy" into the description. But the problem was that I always felt that I had had enough of Adams after the third Hithiker's Guide to the Galaxy book, and whenever I scanned Pratchett's section in the bookstore I was immediately put off by not knowing where to start reading among the approximately five hundred thousand Diskworld books. I'm glad I finally took the time to find out that these two books, The Colour of Magic and The Light Fantastic, jointly comprise the first tale in the series, and that they were definitely worth reading.<br /><br />The Diskworld books are essentially satire of the high fantasy genre, or at least that's the foundation upon which everything else is built. This pair of books follows the misadventures of Rincewind, a utterly inept and thoroughly cowardly wizard, and Twoflowers, a clueless traveler who happens to be in possession of both endless optimism and a magical suitcase that's always wandering off and messily devouring people who get in its way. Things go from bad to worse for the two as divine powers both deliver them into and yank them out of all kinds of fantastic perils.<br /><br />As someone who grew up reading plenty of this kind of thing and playing a lot of Dungeons&amp; Dragons, I'm familiar enough with the genre and trappings that Pratchett lampoons. Yes, there's the Conan parody, there's the Dragonriders of Pern tribute, there's the in-joke about Leiber's Fafhrd and Gray Mouser. But that's easy. The thing that made me almost immediately fall in love with these books is the author's dry wit and his ability to derive humor not only from the absurdity of the story (and believe me, it gets plenty absurd) but also from just good old fashioned turns of phrase, wry commentary, and jokes. The guy just has an amazing ability to stuff five or six jokes into a single sentence, most of them making masterful use of that trusty standby of British humor, irony. It's really smart and really funny, and the fact that it builds on the inherent silliness of the high fantasy genre is just icing.<br /><br />I should also note how imaginative Pratchett is, which is a useful quality given his subject matter. He bounces his heroes from one (generally horrible and dangerous) situation to another at a frantic pace, and his ability to come up with new material and new situations amazes me. And while many of them are obvious parodies of fantasy staples, just as many seem to be wholly new creations. As one small (and obligatory) example, the Diskworld itself is a flat coin of a world that rides atop four enormous elephants, who themselves ride on the back of a colossal turtle with two continent-sized flippers that it uses to swim slowly through the cold reaches of space.<br /><br />But at the same time, if I have one complaint about these first two books, it's that they're almost maniacal in their plotting. While it's nice to see Pratchett's considerable imagination and humor on display as we go from situation to situation, the first book reads like an extended doodle with little plot and a whole "gods playing games with mortals" subtext that's entirely dropped in the next book. There's also one Conan the Barbarian parody that's abruptly dropped in favor of another Conan the Barbarian parody who Pratchett apparently liked better. It's not until the latter part of the second book does an overall plot come into play, but honestly I was enjoying myself so much I really didn't mind. Expect to see lots more Discworld books reviewed here in the future. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2932020423926860904">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1975474883712559345">Tried to start him at the beginning, as many of my dear friends love him. However, this book showed no particular charm nor skill of construction. It is an early piece, so this unpractised work is to be expected. The jokes were more worthy of groans than guffaws, and I was left feeling rather let down, since he's been compared to the superlatively funny <a title="Douglas Adams" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4.Douglas_Adams">Douglas Adams</a>.<br /><br />After finding this one dull, a friend suggested I try one of his later books, so I started <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1195372">Moving Pictures</a>, which was better craft</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1975474883712559345">Tried to start him at the beginning, as many of my dear friends love him. However, this book showed no particular charm nor skill of construction. It is an early piece, so this unpractised work is to be expected. The jokes were more worthy of groans than guffaws, and I was left feeling rather let down, since he's been compared to the superlatively funny <a title="Douglas Adams" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4.Douglas_Adams">Douglas Adams</a>.<br /><br />After finding this one dull, a friend suggested I try one of his later books, so I started <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1195372">Moving Pictures</a>, which was better crafted, but no more amusing. I guess you can't trust your friends.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://starsbeetlesandfools.blogspot.com/2012/06/suggested-readings-in-fantasy.html">My Fantasy Book Suggestions</a></span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1066596066">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11005593811378266837">And so it begins … for me at least. Sir Terry Pratchett’s wildly imaginative Discworld series begins with the 1983 publication of The Color of Magic.<br /><br />I have been reading science fiction and fantasy for a long time and somehow I have managed to not read any of his works. A friend suggested I try one, I’d like it and so I read the fourth in the series, <a title="Mort (Discworld, #4; Death, #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/386372.Mort__Discworld___4__Death___1_">Mort</a> and I thought so much that I decided I would climb the hill and enjoy every step.<br /><br />Begin with a heaping portion of British humor (humour), mix in</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11005593811378266837">And so it begins … for me at least. Sir Terry Pratchett’s wildly imaginative Discworld series begins with the 1983 publication of The Color of Magic.<br /><br />I have been reading science fiction and fantasy for a long time and somehow I have managed to not read any of his works. A friend suggested I try one, I’d like it and so I read the fourth in the series, <a title="Mort (Discworld, #4; Death, #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/386372.Mort__Discworld___4__Death___1_">Mort</a> and I thought so much that I decided I would climb the hill and enjoy every step.<br /><br />Begin with a heaping portion of British humor (humour), mix in a share of Douglas Adams, sprinkle liberally with Monty Python, throw in a fantastic amount of fantasy from the Piers Anthony brand of fiction and top with a wink and a nod and you have Terry Pratchett Discworld embarkation. The Potent Voyager has set sail and much mirth and irreverence is certainly to follow.<br /><br /><img width="400" height="400" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437256933i/15559392.png" /></span>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1260027141">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1708719784113229833"><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395015i/760700._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429904912i/14642193._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429904912i/14642194._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br />A charming and sometimes tedious novel, Rincewind grew on me quickly and I enjoyed watching him get into and out of scrapes along the way. Death's and Fate's frustration with him was hilarious. I kept imagining them as toddlers stomping their feet :-D.<br /><br />Two Flower I was so so on... sometimes he charmed me and others... eh. His optimism seemed misplaced sometimes, but he had good intentions.<br /><br />A nice start to the series, plenty of action and some humor :) The scenes with Krull and near the edge of the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1708719784113229833"><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395015i/760700._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429904912i/14642193._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429904912i/14642194._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br />A charming and sometimes tedious novel, Rincewind grew on me quickly and I enjoyed watching him get into and out of scrapes along the way. Death's and Fate's frustration with him was hilarious. I kept imagining them as toddlers stomping their feet :-D.<br /><br />Two Flower I was so so on... sometimes he charmed me and others... eh. His optimism seemed misplaced sometimes, but he had good intentions.<br /><br />A nice start to the series, plenty of action and some humor :) The scenes with Krull and near the edge of the world were one of my many favorites... I sympathize with Rincewind and the vertigo sensation of looking over the edge *shudders* I'd rather stay on land thanks.<br /><br />It seemed alot to cram into one novel, at times my eyes glazed over and I had to re-read a couple passages. Don't get me wrong, it was all interesting but it could've been spread out more.<br /><br />An enjoyable ride nonetheless, this world is one I wouldn't mind living in and/or visit from time to time. Hats off to you once again Mr. Pratchett for bringing this to us :)<br /><br />Read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/43865685">David's excellent review</a> , he captures it wonderfully.<br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421940798i/13432097.png" /><br /><br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_29152549">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29152549" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1219253-amanda" class="left imgcol" title="Amanda"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1411956191p2/1219253.jpg" alt="Amanda" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/29152549?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 25, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1219253-amanda" class="user" title="Amanda">Amanda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic" title="Hardcover 9780060855925" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1219253-amanda?shelf=meh" class="actionLinkLite">meh</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1219253-amanda?shelf=blog" class="actionLinkLite">blog</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer29152549">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14432278661700283519">Meh. It just didn't do it for me. Unfortunately, this book has been recommended to me so many times by well-meaning friends who know my love of absurd British humor that it couldn't possibly live up to the hype. It suffers from <em>The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy</em> syndrome. For years, everyone I knew--friends, family, students, co-workers--would ask me if I had read <em>Hitchhiker's</em> and their mouths would drop when I admitted no, I hadn't . . . yet. Their response was always the same, "Oh, but you h</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14432278661700283519">Meh. It just didn't do it for me. Unfortunately, this book has been recommended to me so many times by well-meaning friends who know my love of absurd British humor that it couldn't possibly live up to the hype. It suffers from <em>The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy</em> syndrome. For years, everyone I knew--friends, family, students, co-workers--would ask me if I had read <em>Hitchhiker's</em> and their mouths would drop when I admitted no, I hadn't . . . yet. Their response was always the same, "Oh, but you have to! It's like it was written for YOU!" By the time I got around to reading it, there's no way it could have lived up to the expectations that had been percolating for years. Ditto for <em>The Color of Magic</em>. <br /><br />I'll admit, Pratchett has a way with words and there was the occasional turn of phrase in response to which I made that air-escaping-from-the-nose sound that's not full bodied enough to be considered a snort of laughter. There was the infrequent half-smile. A few head nods in appreciation of a clever conceit. But, alas, there were no tear-inducing uncontrollable fits of laughter, which is what I expected. Will I read more Pratchett? Yes, because I have at least three more books by him lying about. I just hope they're better than this.<br /><br />Cross posted at <a rel="nofollow" href="http://viiamanda.blogspot.com/">This Insignificant Cinder</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14432278661700283519">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_146424481">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146424481" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1376766-becky" class="left imgcol" title="Becky"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1446571694p2/1376766.jpg" alt="Becky" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/146424481?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 24, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1376766-becky" class="user" title="Becky">Becky</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic" title="Hardcover 9780060855925" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=multi-dimensional" class="actionLinkLite">multi-dimensional</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=disappointing" class="actionLinkLite">disappointing</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=ebook_nook" class="actionLinkLite">ebook_nook</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2014" class="actionLinkLite">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer146424481">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10657266752428191102">I dunno if this is going to be a proper 'review' (heh, as though any of the things that I write in this space are...), it'll likely just be a bunch of randomness and ranting. So, like my usual offerings.<br /><br />I read Amanda's review (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29152549">This'un.</a>) and I'm all like "Yep." This is one of those books/series that people love and it makes me want to love it and then I set crazy goals for myself, like reading them... all... in a year... just maybe not this one... and then when the first one ends up NOT being the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10657266752428191102">I dunno if this is going to be a proper 'review' (heh, as though any of the things that I write in this space are...), it'll likely just be a bunch of randomness and ranting. So, like my usual offerings.<br /><br />I read Amanda's review (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29152549">This'un.</a>) and I'm all like "Yep." This is one of those books/series that people love and it makes me want to love it and then I set crazy goals for myself, like reading them... all... in a year... just maybe not this one... and then when the first one ends up NOT being the fucking greatest thing since ever, I feel disappointed. It's unfair. (To me, I mean. I don't care if it's fair to the book if others have set my expectations too high and then it didn't live up to them. It's a book. It doesn't have feelings or a brain and thus cannot understand why it should feel sorry for me.)<br /><br />But, to be fair to the expectation raisers, I'd also read Good Omens by Neil Gaiman and Terry Pratchett, and I really enjoyed it, so that also tended to set the bar higher and make my fall just that much further. Sadface.<br /><br />Anyway. So, in a discussion with a friend, she mentioned that "The Colour of Magic is basically a collection of in-jokes about other books." Which goes a long way toward explaining why it didn't work for me. <br /><br />1) Because, of the authors mentioned whose work is being joked upon or referenced or whatever, I've read very little to none at all, and therefore would be quite the opposite of the intended audience, if, as I would presume, the audience is intended to get the jokes and/or references. <br /><br />2) I just really dislike this kind of homework prerequisite reading thing. Zelazny did the same thing with A Night In The Lonesome October, and even though I had read much more of the referenced and hinted at works he incorporated into his story, and so should have been more "in the know" and thus able to enjoy it more, I didn't. I don't read that way. I am not analyzing every line looking for something else - I'm looking for the author to tell me a story. And this kind of storytelling is both lazy and too much work at the same time, if you ask me. <br /><br />Don't get me wrong, I like easter eggs in books. I do. I like little references that people in the know will get and have a little something added... it's nice. I like it. But, in my opinion, it should just be that - a little something nice added. People who don't get the reference should not even notice it, because the story is standing on its own legs and is complete without it. If the story doesn't make sense ON ITS OWN, and if I need to have read an entire genre or two's worth of books just to follow the events in your story - I'm not going to enjoy it. I don't read to interpret A to be a reference to X from book Q and need to know X from Q's history to understand what A is doing in your book. I just want a good fucking story. Tell me one, and get on with it. <br /><br />But about the book itself, I dunno what to say. It didn't feel like a novel, which was how I approached it, it felt like a set of stories just sharing some characters and a general world setting. I think trying to read it as a novel, looking for the overarching story from page 1 to page 200-whatever, set me up for failure as well. If I had read this as each chapter being a vignette story, that would probably have been better. <br /><br />Likewise, it just seemed to forget some of the conflicts that were raised. In the beginning of the book, the Patriarch (or whatever he's called) threatens Rincewind with death if anything untoward should happen to Twoflower the tourist... but that passes like a leaf in the wind and nothing ever comes of it and is never mentioned again. In fact, every danger is just gone as soon as its gone. There's no follow-up, there's no consequences... heck, most of the time there's no rational, logical reason that anything happens (or doesn't happen) in the first place. And that is one of my least favorite things. I hate when there are no rules and anything and everything and the kitchen sink are just possible because why not? It's <em>WHIMSICAL!</em> -_- <br /><br />Grrrrr. So annoying. It was like 200 pages of deus ex machina. <br /><br />I didn't care about any of the characters I think I was meant to care about. I liked Death, and the Luggage. I was rooting for them both to take their due from Rincewind. Maybe next book. By all accounts, the Discworld books get better, and I'll probably go along and hope for that, but my patience has thinned quite a lot. I'll give this series another chance, but if it continues on this way - with the references and the deus ex machina in place of proper storytelling, and the unfunny (because man, I didn't even crack a smile!), I'm writing it off. Life is too short.<br /><br />2 Stars for POTENTIAL, and I'm being generous here.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10657266752428191102">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_521979658">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/521979658" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/811928-forrest" class="left imgcol" title="Forrest"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442457426p2/811928.jpg" alt="Forrest" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/521979658?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 13, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/811928-forrest" class="user" title="Forrest">Forrest</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer521979658">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4167499118077503138">I read this book way back in high school, when I lived in England. Having forgotten everything except for the fact that there was a trunk that liked to eat people, I bought the book (again) to see how it stood up these many years later. As I've read I've received goodreads messages and been spoken to by several people who have warned me that Pratchett was just warming up with this one, that he hadn't reached his highest form yet. I still have to read more of his work (I'm planning on <em>Mort</em> and <em>Gu</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4167499118077503138">I read this book way back in high school, when I lived in England. Having forgotten everything except for the fact that there was a trunk that liked to eat people, I bought the book (again) to see how it stood up these many years later. As I've read I've received goodreads messages and been spoken to by several people who have warned me that Pratchett was just warming up with this one, that he hadn't reached his highest form yet. I still have to read more of his work (I'm planning on <em>Mort</em> and <em>Guards! Guards!</em>), so I have no benchmark to measure against other than what I thought in high school versus what I think now. And while the book is funny, it's not as hilarious as I remember it. I've probably become a little jaded since those days, which is more a reflection of me and my experiences than it is of Pratchett and his writing. <br /><br />That's not to say that the book was bad, it wasn't. In fact, it's got some moments of pure brilliance and was, in some ways, much more well-written than I had expected. The exchange between the Arch Astronomer of Krull and Goldeneyes Dactylos smacks strongly of the sort of humor one would expect in a <a rel="nofollow" href="http://forrestaguirre.blogspot.com/2012/09/my-man-jeeves.html">Jeeves and Wooster</a> story. And that is the highest compliment I think I can give to a piece of humorous writing. The section on the Wyrmberg sniffed in <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.multiverse.org/">Michael Moorcock's</a> direction. And at least a couple of the characters were spoofs of two of my favorites: <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/332920023">Fafhrd and Grey Mouser</a>.<br /><br />I must admit that I also liked Rincewind, the bungling wizard. Some have labelled him a coward. I'd call him . . . normal. Someone like you or me: allergic to pain, justifiably afraid of being dropped from great heights, fearful of fear itself, and yet he commits himself to get done what needs to get done when it really matters . . . most of the time. Unlike, say, Gandalf, Rincewind is full of foible and, as a result, a really loveable character. At least he was for me. I feel for the guy. Sometimes what I'm feeling is embarrassment, but I feel for him.<br /><br />Poor Rincewind. I do hope to see him again.<br /><br />Twoflower, the other main character, I liked at the beginning, but by the end of the book he seems to have become rather withdrawn and almost a touch (just a touch) sullen. I couldn't figure out why he changed so much through the book, so I'm left to speculate.<br /><br />Maybe he became jaded after high school, just like me.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4167499118077503138">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer498543420">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16413926042559060802">Zany, wild, preposterous, and oh so fun—I understand the Discworld hype and see why it's such a fan favourite.<br /><br />But underneath all the light humour is clever trope subversion and a sense that Pratchett knows exactly what he's doing, more so than just a few laughs.<br /><br />This first installment isn't an immediate favourite, but it's a promising start to a series I'm looking forward to reading. I know there are a ton of Discworld reading guides out there, but I'm a stickler for published order and I'm going</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16413926042559060802">Zany, wild, preposterous, and oh so fun—I understand the Discworld hype and see why it's such a fan favourite.<br /><br />But underneath all the light humour is clever trope subversion and a sense that Pratchett knows exactly what he's doing, more so than just a few laughs.<br /><br />This first installment isn't an immediate favourite, but it's a promising start to a series I'm looking forward to reading. I know there are a ton of Discworld reading guides out there, but I'm a stickler for published order and I'm going with that.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1269798834">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1269798834" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words" class="left imgcol" title="Evelyn (devours and digests words)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1443086847p2/38658747.jpg" alt="Evelyn (devours and digests words)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1269798834?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 07, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words" class="user" title="Evelyn (devours and digests words)">Evelyn (devours and digests words)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11138378-the-colour-of-magic" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People looking for a bag full of laughs with a cynical view, and tons of fun, fun, fun adventure</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Evelyn (devours and digests words) by: </span>
      Fabian, Ryan
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=great-characterization" class="actionLinkLite">great-characterization</a>,

              <a href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=writing-i-would-love-to-imitate" class="actionLinkLite">writing-i-would-love-to-imitate</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=bagful-of-laughs" class="actionLinkLite">bagful-of-laughs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1269798834">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3295350410069817816"><blockquote>Magic never dies. It merely fades away. </blockquote><br /><br />I first visited the world of Discworld at the age of twelve when I was still wolfing down picture books and fingering through easy-peasy written books. Then one day, I saw a friend prancing around with this book to classes. I have a sharp eye on colourful book covers and this one's won me over. I <s>demanded</s> asked to borrow this and right on the spot, he let me.<br /><br />Back home I immediately flipped to page one. Upon the first few paragraphs however, my brain went d</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3295350410069817816"><blockquote>Magic never dies. It merely fades away. </blockquote><br /><br />I first visited the world of Discworld at the age of twelve when I was still wolfing down picture books and fingering through easy-peasy written books. Then one day, I saw a friend prancing around with this book to classes. I have a sharp eye on colourful book covers and this one's won me over. I <s>demanded</s> asked to borrow this and right on the spot, he let me.<br /><br />Back home I immediately flipped to page one. Upon the first few paragraphs however, my brain went dead.<br /><br />Has someone ever tell you a joke that is supposed to be funny but you just don't get the meaning? That was how it was like with this book. I didn't get the humour and the worldbuilding was much too intricate for me to swallow.<br /><br />So in the end, I gave up after 15+ pages in. The next few days after my defeat, the book was returned back to its owner. I did not look back after that. <br /><br />Six years later, I revisited Discworld, and I can safely say that I absolutely love the adventures this time. <strong>The worldbuilding took a while to piece itself together but when it did, the final image is fantastic and utterly magical. </strong><br /><br />Imagine a whole world being carried on the backs of four elephants standing on the shell of a large, gigantic turtle (sex undertermined) as it moves slowly throughout space.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1441619947i/16130234.jpg" /><br /><br />Bizzare, isn't it?<br /><br />That is what I would describe the whole story. Bizzare, and completely <em>out-of-the-blue. </em><br /><br />Rincewind who's an incompetent, dull-witted wizard found himself acting as a tour guide for the naive, gullible, and painfully optimistic Twoflower who had just arrived in Ankh-Morpork hoping for an unforgettable adventure. Armed with a hundred-legged Luggage that can snap and bite, a bag full of gold and a picture box (camera), he is the very image of a tourist except with the label 'KIDNAP ME AND TAKE ALL MY GOLD' slapped on his forehead. When Twoflower got kidnapped for his money, Rincewind was forced to rescue the fellow.<br /><br /><blockquote>
<em>Tourists</em>, Rincewind decided, meant <em>Idiot</em>.</blockquote><br /><br /><a title="The Colour of Magic The Illustrated Screenplay by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/833512.The_Colour_of_Magic_The_Illustrated_Screenplay">The Colour of Magic</a> is a series of adventures and unfortunate events between a cynic wizard and a happy-go-lucky tourist.<br /><br />I don't think I've ever laughed this hard after <a title="Good Omens The Nice and Accurate Prophecies of Agnes Nutter, Witch by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12067.Good_Omens_The_Nice_and_Accurate_Prophecies_of_Agnes_Nutter__Witch"> Good Omens</a>, another fun satirical book. The story is always delivered in full humour, always even when things turn a wee bit grim. This time though,<strong> the witty remarks are not lost on me.</strong> <br /><br /><strong>Much like the title promised, the book is full of colour and magic </strong>(don't expect too much from Rincewind though. He may be a wizard but he only knew one spell).<strong> It never failed to keep me on my toes with its fantasy elements that keep pouring in.</strong> There are dryads, elves, dragons you must imagine to conjour to life, a walking Luggage, an imp who paint pictures, a talking sword, hydrophobic wizards, gods, goddesses, and DEATH Himself. <br /><br />Adventures after  adventures! If you want a fun read then this book is something to be reckoned with.<br /><br /><blockquote>'It was octarine, the colour of magic. It was alive and glowing and vibrant and it was the undisputed pigment of the imagination, because wherever it appeared it was a sign that mere matter was a servant of the powers of the magical mind. It was enchantment itself.<br />But Rincewind always thought it looked a sort of greenish-purple.'</blockquote><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3295350410069817816">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16490915127497928606">This was a fun, quick read. I enjoyed it and plan to read my way through disc world. This somewhat cartoonish seeming universe is populated by colorful and unlikely characters. The author created an original and interesting mythology and multiverse. <br />Hidden within the tongue and cheek humor and somewhat silly action is an intelligence and insightful view of not just those make believe world, but ours as well. Many references are to actual occult concepts and the magic, while loose, humorous and e</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16490915127497928606">This was a fun, quick read. I enjoyed it and plan to read my way through disc world. This somewhat cartoonish seeming universe is populated by colorful and unlikely characters. The author created an original and interesting mythology and multiverse. <br />Hidden within the tongue and cheek humor and somewhat silly action is an intelligence and insightful view of not just those make believe world, but ours as well. Many references are to actual occult concepts and the magic, while loose, humorous and entertaining, also has real world conceptual connections that make for interesting, between the lines, reading.<br />Much of this story is chasing and running, which does get tiresome at times, but the book finds its salvation in its creativity and individualism.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1282647406">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1282647406" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/30410174-mangrii" class="left imgcol" title="Mangrii"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1423216327p2/30410174.jpg" alt="Mangrii" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1282647406?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 21, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/30410174-mangrii" class="user" title="Mangrii">Mangrii</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/789326.El_color_de_la_magia" title="Paperback 9788497596794" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1282647406">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7627474001167570118">Por fin me he puesto con el reto que tenía entre manos, comenzar desde el inicio la saga Mundodisco del fallecido Terry Pratchett; aunque ya había leído algún volumen suelto (porque en esta saga poco importa el orden en realidad), en esta ocasión quiero seguir el orden de publicación.<br />En este primer volumen nos narran a través de cuatro capítulos la historia de Dosflores, un singular turista de una lejano Imperio que desea conocer a los famosos héroes de Mundodisco, vivir emocionantes aventuras y</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7627474001167570118">Por fin me he puesto con el reto que tenía entre manos, comenzar desde el inicio la saga Mundodisco del fallecido Terry Pratchett; aunque ya había leído algún volumen suelto (porque en esta saga poco importa el orden en realidad), en esta ocasión quiero seguir el orden de publicación.<br />En este primer volumen nos narran a través de cuatro capítulos la historia de Dosflores, un singular turista de una lejano Imperio que desea conocer a los famosos héroes de Mundodisco, vivir emocionantes aventuras y realizar recuerdos o cuadros de la ciudad más grande y corrupta, Ankh-Mopork. Gracias a ello iremos conociendo todo un elenco de simpáticos personajes como son el fracasado mago que solo sabe un hechizo Rincewind, la graciosa Muerte, el guerrero bárbaro Hrun y algunos de los dioses de Mundodisco más poderosos como son Dama y Sino.<br />Cada capítulo es totalmente diferente, aunque tienen como hilo conductor las peripecias de Dosflores y Rincewind; aventuras en las que Pratchett va haciendo pequeños homenajes a obras clásicas de la fantasía como Dragonlance o Conan. Es estilo de Pratchett es espectacular, sobre todo por la forma directa que tiene y como te hace prestar atención a lo claramente importante de lo que está narrando. Eso sí, es un estilo un tanto loco de contar historias, aderezado con bastante humor inglés y donde cada párrafo o descripción desborda imaginación con escenas la mar de divertidas, descabelladas y completamente absurdas en algunas ocasiones.<br />Lo que encontré negativo en esta novela es que al principio estamos totalmente perdidos, no entendemos la mitad de lo que nos está contando, o al menos así fue en mi caso. Luego comienzas a comprender como van las cosas en Mundodisco, el disco con una cúpula azul apoyado sobre 4 gigantescos elefantes y a su vez sobre la Gran Tortuga A´Tuin; donde la magia, el color y los números tienen mucha importancia; un mundo habitado por héroes, dioses, dragones imaginarios, trolls y un sinfín de criaturas.<br />Sin duda quiero continuar con la saga, aunque son 40 volúmenes y creo que me llevará la vida, de pronto creo que enseguida caerá el segundo, ya que quiero saber cómo continúan las andanzas de Rincewind y compañía.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7627474001167570118">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer225223494">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9847257272783967262">This was the perfect pick me up after the depressing, depressing, depressing downer if The Road by Cormac McCarthy. I laughed out loud reading this and that is not something I do very often. Rincewind is a new favorite character and Terry Pratchett is a new favorite author. I'm not sure I would have loved this as much I I hadn't been in the perfect mood for it. But, I was in the perfect mood and I did love it. </span>

              <a href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2014" class="actionLinkLite">read-2014</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer466064953">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6242443808249126368"><strong>Executive Summary:</strong> Started slow, but finished strong.<br /><br /><strong> <u>Full Review</u> </strong><br />I've been meaning to read Discworld for awhile. A good friend of mine loves the series and recommended it to me over 10 years ago, but I just never got around to it.<br /><br />He suggested I might be better off starting with <a title="Guards! Guards! (Discworld, #8) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64216.Guards__Guards___Discworld___8_">Guards! Guards!</a> than this book. However between picking up the first few books on a sale, and my general need to read thing in publication order.<br /><br />My understanding is that while all the books are set in Discworld, there ar</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6242443808249126368"><strong>Executive Summary:</strong> Started slow, but finished strong.<br /><br /><strong>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</strong><br />I've been meaning to read Discworld for awhile. A good friend of mine loves the series and recommended it to me over 10 years ago, but I just never got around to it.<br /><br />He suggested I might be better off starting with <a title="Guards! Guards! (Discworld, #8) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64216.Guards__Guards___Discworld___8_">Guards! Guards!</a> than this book. However between picking up the first few books on a sale, and my general need to read thing in publication order.<br /><br />My understanding is that while all the books are set in Discworld, there are several different sub-series with recurring characters. The <a title="Guards! Guards! (Discworld, #8) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64216.Guards__Guards___Discworld___8_">Guards! Guards!</a> one is supposed to be a different set I guess. I don't pretend to know enough about it. I do know there are big complicated charts on the whole thing.<br /><br />I found this book a slow start. I was expecting things to be a lot funnier. I'm not sure if I just wasn't getting them, or they weren't as prevalent.<br /><br />It took me awhile to get through the story. I didn't really care too much for Rincewind or Twoflower. The luggage however was pretty amusing.<br /><br />It all changed for me in the last quarter or so though. I was really cracking up at some of the jokes and overall was reading at a much faster pace.<br /><br />All and all it's enough to get to try the next one at some point, which is good considering I already own it. Hopefully I work may way up to <a title="Guards! Guards! (Discworld, #8) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64216.Guards__Guards___Discworld___8_">Guards! Guards!</a> to see if I like that more.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_78912175">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78912175" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1283483-steven-harbin" class="left imgcol" title="Steven Harbin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1307406902p2/1283483.jpg" alt="Steven Harbin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/78912175?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 10, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1283483-steven-harbin" class="user" title="Steven Harbin">Steven Harbin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic" title="Hardcover 9780060855925" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1283483-steven-harbin?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1283483-steven-harbin?shelf=humor" class="actionLinkLite">humor</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1283483-steven-harbin?shelf=owned" class="actionLinkLite">owned</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1283483-steven-harbin?shelf=read-2000-to-2009" class="actionLinkLite">read-2000-to-2009</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1283483-steven-harbin?shelf=series" class="actionLinkLite">series</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1283483-steven-harbin?shelf=discworld" class="actionLinkLite">discworld</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1283483-steven-harbin?shelf=read-in-2009" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2009</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1283483-steven-harbin?shelf=read-previously-re-reading" class="actionLinkLite">read-previously-re-reading</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer78912175">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8523710332080245337">Although this is the first book in the Discworld series, it's actually the 2nd I've completed, <a title="The Wee Free Men (Discworld, #30) (Tiffany Aching, #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34494.The_Wee_Free_Men__Discworld___30___Tiffany_Aching___1_">The Wee Free Men</a> being the first. I enjoyed this book, although having read a later book in the series showed me that Mr. Pratchett's writing has improved considerably over time. Still, this is a fun read for anyone who likes fantasy in general and humorous fantasy in particular. I came to really like inept magician Rincewind and his traveling companion Twoflower, first tourist in Discworld history (ap</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8523710332080245337">Although this is the first book in the Discworld series, it's actually the 2nd I've completed, <a title="The Wee Free Men (Discworld, #30) (Tiffany Aching, #1) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34494.The_Wee_Free_Men__Discworld___30___Tiffany_Aching___1_">The Wee Free Men</a> being the first. I enjoyed this book, although having read a later book in the series showed me that Mr. Pratchett's writing has improved considerably over time. Still, this is a fun read for anyone who likes fantasy in general and humorous fantasy in particular. I came to really like inept magician Rincewind and his traveling companion Twoflower, first tourist in Discworld history (apparently) and caught several parodies of other famous fantasy works in the adventures the two men had while traversing Discworld. If you've read any of <a title="Leiber Fritz" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/32627.Leiber_Fritz">Leiber Fritz</a>'s works or those of <a title="Robert E. Howard" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/66700.Robert_E__Howard">Robert E. Howard</a> you'll see what I mean. Probably there are many other allusions I've have caught if I was more well read in modern fantasy authors. But the novel is more than just a parody of other fantasies. There's some highly original stuff in this very first Discworld novel that would have been enough to arouse my interest in continuing reading the series, even if I hadn't already read a later book. My favorite is the Luggage, whom I want for a pet even if it does have some homicical tendencies.<br /><br />I recommend this book to anyone who likes fantasy, humor, humorous fantasy, parody, and just good writing. I've even recommended it to friends who don't normally read fantasy. A solid 4 out of 5 stars.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8523710332080245337">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1110681682">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16245155346621362111">I enjoy reading science fiction and fantasy, but my mother always says that she does not. She claims that in this sort of book, the author can allow the characters to do "anything", and there are no set rules for the natural world to obey. I generally disagree with her. Good science fiction and fantasy authors invent a world, and they invent the parameters of the possible, and stick within those limits.<br /><br />However, in this book, I must say, <em>anything</em> goes. There are no limits to the magic; it is boun</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16245155346621362111">I enjoy reading science fiction and fantasy, but my mother always says that she does not. She claims that in this sort of book, the author can allow the characters to do "anything", and there are no set rules for the natural world to obey. I generally disagree with her. Good science fiction and fantasy authors invent a world, and they invent the parameters of the possible, and stick within those limits.<br /><br />However, in this book, I must say, <em>anything</em> goes. There are no limits to the magic; it is boundless and thoroughly unpredictable. This book is a hilarious spoof on the fantasy genre. One of the two main characters, Rincewind, is a failed magician. He only knows a single spell. Yet so much magic happens to him, and he eludes the clutches of fate and death so often, that there must be something magical about him. It is pure, no-holds-barred, fantasy. Every page holds a surprise.<br /><br />And the surprises are simply hilarious. Rincewind found a frog who asked to be put down on the floor. After the frog was put on the floor, there was a magical tornado spewing magical colors and lightning, and noises, and the frog turned into...a frog! Then comes a goddess, who "comes only when not invoked."<br /><br />Rincewind finds himself acting as a tour guide for rich out-of-towner tourist named Twoflower. He tries to guide Twoflower through the most evil, dangerous, crime-filled city named "Morpork". Twoflower wants to experience everything, including brawls, fights, dragons, and an unspeakable soul-eater. And he wants to capture his experiences in pictures--he carries around a box that takes pictures. It's not a camera--it's a box with an artistic homunculus inside. At one point, Rincewind says: <blockquote>"When I said harness I didn't mean harness," snapped Rincewind. "I meant, well. I just meant that--I dunno, I just can't think of the right words. I just think the world ought to be more sort of organized."<br /><br />"That's just fantasy," said Twoflower.</blockquote></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16245155346621362111">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
