<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_79775018">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/79775018" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin" class="left imgcol" title="Mike (the Paladin)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1450193915p2/2187043.jpg" alt="Mike (the Paladin)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/79775018?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 24, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin" class="user" title="Mike (the Paladin)">Mike (the Paladin)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/200711.The_Colour_of_Magic" title="Hardcover 9780861403240" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer79775018">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14144431032595448952">Ahh, the story of Twoflower and the "failed" wizard Rincewind. Although calling Rincewind a "failed" wizard is possibly not really fair to him as he's only a "failed" wizard because having sneaked a look at a forbidden spell book one the 8 Great Spells has taken up the room in his brain that would be needed for other spells and he can't get it out, at least not without casting it, and since neither he nor the other wizards know what it will do...destroy the world, the universe, the multiverse...</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14144431032595448952">Ahh, the story of Twoflower and the "failed" wizard Rincewind. Although calling Rincewind a "failed" wizard is possibly not really fair to him as he's only a "failed" wizard because having sneaked a look at a forbidden spell book one the 8 Great Spells has taken up the room in his brain that would be needed for other spells and he can't get it out, at least not without casting it, and since neither he nor the other wizards know what it will do...destroy the world, the universe, the multiverse...or possibly something less drastic, it doesn't seem like the best option.<br /><br />Anyway Rincewind becomes the guide (at a wage so high as to be mythical) to the Disc World's first tourist (and possibly last as he seems bent on getting himself and Rincewind killed).<br /><br />Pratchett has a wonderful turn of phrase and an oddly quirky mind that is endlessly inventive.<br /><br />I want to comment on something else here also. It seems that most who write Synopses (I always feel that should be "synopsi")anyway, they seem to think that a great thing to say about a book is that it is "irreverent"it is I believe said about almost all Pratchett's work in almost every synopsis. Okay, I'm a Christian and while Sir Terry is apparently more on the atheistic side of things I detect no rancor in his work. Yes he skewers the idiosyncrasies of religions in general and some things in specific but I don't ever get a since of "hate" or even condescension. I have enjoyed several of his works and while I would almost undoubtedly disagree with him on these things, I don't think I would dislike him and I don't think he "dislikes" people simply on the grounds that they are religious.<br /><br />Judge for yourself.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14144431032595448952">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_14406375">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14406375" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/837414-belarius" class="left imgcol" title="Belarius"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1201416847p2/837414.jpg" alt="Belarius" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/14406375?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 06, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/837414-belarius" class="user" title="Belarius">Belarius</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic" title="Hardcover 9780060855925" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Obsessive Completionists</span></div>

        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer14406375">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9523819967837735821">Author Terry Pratchett may be the modern day Mark Twain, one of the most prolific satirical authors in genre fiction. The world he spins his elaborate metaphors is that of Discworld, a setting in which he has successfully parodied everything from opera to religion, from currency to war, from morris dancing to mall proliferation. But before Discworld was a template upon which all things modern could be parodied, it was simply a parody, and a mediocre one at best.<br /><br />Pratchett's humor is similar in ma</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9523819967837735821">Author Terry Pratchett may be the modern day Mark Twain, one of the most prolific satirical authors in genre fiction. The world he spins his elaborate metaphors is that of Discworld, a setting in which he has successfully parodied everything from opera to religion, from currency to war, from morris dancing to mall proliferation. But before Discworld was a template upon which all things modern could be parodied, it was simply a parody, and a mediocre one at best.<br /><br />Pratchett's humor is similar in many ways to the humor of the late Douglas Adams: it relies heavily on description and implication. Pratchett's ability to tell a coherent story is relatively recent, but his talent for hilarious description in service of a theme stretches further back. With The Color (or, more correctly, Colour) of Magic, Pratchett is only just learning his trade and is still wearing the water wings.<br /><br />Don't mistake this for a negative review: The Colour of Magic is certainly funny, especially if you've read more Dungeons &amp; Dragons spinoff novels than you're willing to admit in public. But it's a lot <em>less</em> funny than almost any other book set in the Discworld, of which there are currently a staggering 36 volumes.<br /><br />If you're the type who must read all the books in a series and must do so in order, <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.craphound.com/images/discworldreadingguide.jpg">here's a (slightly outdated) guide</a>. If not, you may be better served by first learning how awesome the Discworld is (<a title=" Small Gods" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Small%20Gods"> Small Gods</a> and <a title=" Reaper Man" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Reaper%20Man"> Reaper Man</a> are especially good) and then figuring out how completely you want to explore it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9523819967837735821">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_168812577">

  <a href="/user/show/5454475-tfitoby" class="left imgcol" title="Tfitoby"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1342170152p2/5454475.jpg" alt="Tfitoby" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/168812577?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 03, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5454475-tfitoby" class="user" title="Tfitoby">Tfitoby</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/601238.The_Colour_of_Magic" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780552124751" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5454475-tfitoby?shelf=fantastical" class="actionLinkLite">fantastical</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5454475-tfitoby?shelf=funny" class="actionLinkLite">funny</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer168812577">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16211863945660561255"><strong>A fun parody of the fantasy genre and some great world building</strong><br /><br />I've been listening to this one for the past two weeks, I found myself out of shape and in need of something that would hold my concentration whilst I taught my body to exercise again. Ordinarily I'm not a fan of audiobooks but it seemed like the perfect way and the perfect time to get started on the great Discworld re-read that I've had planned for the past two years. It worked.<br /><br />It's been many, many years since I last read this book,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16211863945660561255"><strong>A fun parody of the fantasy genre and some great world building</strong><br /><br />I've been listening to this one for the past two weeks, I found myself out of shape and in need of something that would hold my concentration whilst I taught my body to exercise again. Ordinarily I'm not a fan of audiobooks but it seemed like the perfect way and the perfect time to get started on the great Discworld re-read that I've had planned for the past two years. It worked.<br /><br />It's been many, many years since I last read this book, infact my last experience of the story was the awful television adaptation and so this was an enjoyable reacquaintance with the story as it should be.<br /><br />I realise now that my previous rating of 5 stars was awarded through rose tinted glasses, there are actually quite a few faults with this novel; it is structured as several interlinked short stories for example, this means there is a large amount of repetition of facts and jokes that got to be a little irritating, but overall it still works as a fun parody of fantasy, an actual fantasy novel and is a great platform in terms of the world that Pratchett created for the next 30+ books that he would write.<br /><br />What I found most interesting was how silly it all is compared to the much tighter, later novels that work as social commentary. This growth of the author and the world is going to be interesting to witness from the seat of my exercise bike whilst I attempt to ignore the pain.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16211863945660561255">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('G3qCXXWbSe4/IaoEDJNdaa/8ttJ8bj9bR5sMW08SMlt+rr2Oh0ldFLP53r9y8rvb5gt1yzWzePEtkgnJg4fEHg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">About Terry Pratchett</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett"><img alt="1654" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1235562205p2/1654.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer8617558975100157051">Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <em>The Carpet People</em>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8617558975100157051">Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <em>The Carpet People</em>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <em>The Color of Magic</em>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <em>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</em>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <em>Good Omens</em>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <em>Nation</em>. Terry published <em>Snuff</em> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8617558975100157051">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Terry Pratchett...</a>
